Salvatore, New York Times Bestselling author<br /><br />The Goths followed a bloodthirsty new leader, one who sought to open the Gates of Hell: Wotan. His immortal power stemmed from human sacrifice and dark sorcery, and no sword could touch him. He rode the winds on a leather-winged steed, whi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10049032085081745818">"David Gemmell tells a tale of very real adventure, the stuff of true epic fantasy."<br />--R. A. Salvatore, New York Times Bestselling author<br /><br />The Goths followed a bloodthirsty new leader, one who sought to open the Gates of Hell: Wotan. His immortal power stemmed from human sacrifice and dark sorcery, and no sword could touch him. He rode the winds on a leather-winged steed, while his armies cut a deadly swath across the northern kingdoms. Even death's icy hand could not stop them.<br /><br />Only Uther Pendragon could save Britannia. To do so he must wield his birthright--Cunobelin's blade, the legendary Sword of Power.<br /><br />But Uther was chained in Hell, the sword lost in swirling Chaos. All hope lay with the warrior known as Revelation, with the magic of the Sipstrassi Stones, and with Anduine, a blind girl possessed of arcane powers. Only if these unlikely allies united could they hope to stop the invincible foe before the world plunged into darkness.</span>

      <a href="/user/show/1760824-graham" class="user" title="Graham">Graham</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <a href="/book/show/781301.Last_Sword_of_Power" title="Paperback 9780345379016" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1760824-graham?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer173016562">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2537594007960901609">Not one of the author's best books, but fans should still enjoy it. This one follows on from GHOST KING and is much of the same, with the myths and legends of Arthurian Britain mixed up with sorcery and demonic creatures. A familiar template for Gemmell, then.<br /><br />This one loses points by having too many characters in a rather jumbled storyline. Most of the characters from the first book come back, a whole new cast are introduced, and to complicate matters even further, when characters die they don't</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2537594007960901609">Not one of the author's best books, but fans should still enjoy it. This one follows on from GHOST KING and is much of the same, with the myths and legends of Arthurian Britain mixed up with sorcery and demonic creatures. A familiar template for Gemmell, then.<br /><br />This one loses points by having too many characters in a rather jumbled storyline. Most of the characters from the first book come back, a whole new cast are introduced, and to complicate matters even further, when characters die they don't really die, their souls are transported instead to a netherworld where they find further adventure. Merely keeping track of where/what and who everybody is (I should mention that other characters have dual personalities and are able to adopt different forms at will) becomes an ordeal in itself.<br /><br />Still, as with every book I've read from this author, THE LAST SWORD OF POWER has guts - and heart. The characters and in particular their motivations are never less than believable. The action scenes are exquisite and the human flaws that propel the protagonists are what makes this book so readable.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2537594007960901609">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6789422559623887117">Though I love Gemmell's succinct prose, his gritty exposition and near complete lack of flowery language rarely inspires a strong emotional reaction from me. To me it is simply a different type of literature than say Tolkien. Yet this novel somehow got a real emotional reaction out of me at the end.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText6789422559623887117">Though I love Gemmell's succinct prose, his gritty exposition and near complete lack of flowery language rarely inspires a strong emotional reaction from me. To me it is simply a different type of literature than say Tolkien. Yet this novel somehow got a real emotional reaction out of me at the end. I was really touched by the sorrow and regret of the characters as they looked back on the mistakes of the past and yearned to have chosen differently, wishing to remove the scars they had caused from the hearts of their loved ones. It was a surprisingly touching to a legend that has been told and retold countlessly. </span>

  <a href="/user/show/3632282-ghoule" class="left imgcol" title="Ghoule"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1290922774p2/3632282.jpg" alt="Ghoule" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1139222623?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 23, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3632282-ghoule" class="user" title="Ghoule">Ghoule</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/11601951-la-derni-re-p-e-de-pouvoir" title=" 9782352945093" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1139222623">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11982304799000544869">Arg!<br /><br />J'ai beau apprécier le style de Gemmell en général, il lui arrive malheureusement de rater son coup.<br /><br />« La dernière épée de pouvoir » me rappelle mon enfance, quand je rassemblais des figurines de plusieurs univers distincts afin de créer l'ultime bataille. Je me demandais du coup « Pourquoi les créateurs de dessins animés ne font pas ça aussi? »<br /><br />Imaginez que Zeus (Culain? Lancelot? Révélation) tape sur Odin (Wotan) avec le roi Uther (Thuro?) Pendragon et son fils Arthur (Cormac?) au milieu? Im</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11982304799000544869">Arg!<br /><br />J'ai beau apprécier le style de Gemmell en général, il lui arrive malheureusement de rater son coup.<br /><br />« La dernière épée de pouvoir » me rappelle mon enfance, quand je rassemblais des figurines de plusieurs univers distincts afin de créer l'ultime bataille. Je me demandais du coup « Pourquoi les créateurs de dessins animés ne font pas ça aussi? »<br /><br />Imaginez que Zeus (Culain? Lancelot? Révélation) tape sur Odin (Wotan) avec le roi Uther (Thuro?) Pendragon et son fils Arthur (Cormac?) au milieu? Imaginez que Guenièvre (Gwen Avar et je ne sais plus quel nom) soit mariée avec Uther (!) et qu'elle ait engendrée Arthur (Culain), mais qu'elle pense avoir été amoureuse de Lancelot (Culain et cie), mais que ce n'était pas le cas, car Lancelot est en fait un survivant de l'Atlantide (!!!) qui vit depuis des millénaires grâce à la Siptraasi, une pierre de régénération magique, tout comme Wotan, Gilgamesh (le fils de Lancelot?!) et la Reine Sorcière qui est en fait... N'IMPORTE QUOI!<br /><br />Je n'arrive même pas à raconter l'histoire ici, tellement c'est incohérent. Il y a un peu de "Highlander" dans tout ça, avec des immortels qui se courent après depuis la nuit des temps.<br /><br />Autre problème, il y a énormément de personnages - même des romains qui viennent de deux siècles avant les événements! - , et tous contribuent à la confusion générale, alors que chez George R. R. Martin (Le Trône de Fer), ce problème a été partiellement résolu grâce à la division des chapitres en fonction d'un personnage principal.<br /><br />Le coup fatal est toutefois porté par l'ajout d'une autre réalité, celle des morts qui voyagent vers l'après-vie... mais de laquelle on peut entrer et ressortir sans trop de mal avec les bonnes attitudes, les bons objectifs et les bons objets. Ça peut fonctionner parfois, mais ici, c'est trop.<br /><br />Au final, le chaos généré nous donne l'impression que « j'ai oublié pourquoi on se tapait dessus ».</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11982304799000544869">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15577633809951029654">Uno dei peggiori romanzi di David Gemmel. Siamo molto lontani dalla bellezza evocativa del ciclo dei Drenai, dall’intensità espressiva di Waylander e dalla forza narrativa de Il Leone di Macedonia. La storia è scialba, manca di un forte motore narrativo e di un vero antagonista che facesse muovere la storia.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText15577633809951029654">Uno dei peggiori romanzi di David Gemmel. Siamo molto lontani dalla bellezza evocativa del ciclo dei Drenai, dall’intensità espressiva di Waylander e dalla forza narrativa de Il Leone di Macedonia. La storia è scialba, manca di un forte motore narrativo e di un vero antagonista che facesse muovere la storia. Il dio-re non ha abbastanza carisma da rendere la lettura mozzafiato, ma tende a essere una figura di sfondo, in potenza terribile ma nei fatti poco presente nell’economia della narrazione. <br />E i personaggi? Non sono riuscita a entrare in empatia con nessuno dei loro, né buoni, né cattivi. Ho avvertito un’iniziale simpatia per Cormac, che poi è diventata indifferenza quando il ragazzo ha iniziato a odiare Culain e Uther senza un vero motivo. Nemmeno la povera Anduine e la sua tragica fine mi hanno commosso, segno che questa volta il maestro Gemmel non è riuscito a scuotermi il cuore – capita! <br />Ho trovato inoltre inutile il viaggio nell’Ade, un oltremondo stranamente simile al nostro, che ha ben poco di trascendentale e di intrigante. <br />Ancora, non ho apprezzato la miscellanea fra i protagonisti del ciclo Bretone e i miti di un passato ancor più remoto – Zeus, Apollo, Gilgamesh. E che dire, del personaggio di Ginevra che viene assimilato a quello di Morgana? <br />“L’ultima spada del potere” e un’ennesima storpiatura del Ciclo Bretone, che poteva anche non essere scritta.<br /></span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1080639569">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16208381722109870624">As a follow-up to Ghost King, Last Sword of Power wasn't bad at all. I'd say it was on par with the first novel. But it didn't really bring anything new to the table. It's difficult to fully enjoy a book when you don't really care for its main characters; I disliked Uther completely. I didn't particularly like Cormac, either. Gian was utterly unlikeable. The eternals were all shadows of their former selves, even Pendarric. There were a few good ideas where, but none of them were fully realised o</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16208381722109870624">As a follow-up to Ghost King, Last Sword of Power wasn't bad at all. I'd say it was on par with the first novel. But it didn't really bring anything new to the table. It's difficult to fully enjoy a book when you don't really care for its main characters; I disliked Uther completely. I didn't particularly like Cormac, either. Gian was utterly unlikeable. The eternals were all shadows of their former selves, even Pendarric. There were a few good ideas where, but none of them were fully realised or followed through significantly. Characters went to places, did things, but there was next to no cause and effect to the whole story. It just felt like a few shorter stories tied together, and I felt engaged with the characters of Galead, Prasamaccus, Severinus and a couple of others, to the point where I wished the book had focused on them as main characters instead. Overall, LSoP is quite fun and readable, but it lacks the polish its ambition tried to achieve. You'll enjoy it, but don't expect the best of Gemmell here.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16208381722109870624">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1385001306">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1385001306" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/36209469-derek" class="left imgcol" title="Derek"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1443666059p2/36209469.jpg" alt="Derek" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1385001306?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 24, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/36209469-derek" class="user" title="Derek">Derek</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/781301.Last_Sword_of_Power" title="Paperback 9780345379016" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/36209469-derek?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1385001306">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10387505482127657507">Gemmell really surprised me with this book and, at the end of this small two-book series of Ghost King and Last Sword of Power, I must admit that overall I really enjoyed the journey. I've read several Drenai books coming into this series and I was not expecting what I got here, Gemmell always writes with a lot of heart but this series has it in spades. Gemmell takes you through his story, it's probably not how you would write it but it doesn't mean you won't enjoy it. I've decided that this rev</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10387505482127657507">Gemmell really surprised me with this book and, at the end of this small two-book series of Ghost King and Last Sword of Power, I must admit that overall I really enjoyed the journey. I've read several Drenai books coming into this series and I was not expecting what I got here, Gemmell always writes with a lot of heart but this series has it in spades. Gemmell takes you through his story, it's probably not how you would write it but it doesn't mean you won't enjoy it. I've decided that this review and rating will cover both books in the series because they really feel like two acts within one story and feel incomplete on their own (unlike the Drenai books I've read). I don't know much about the Arthurian comparisons so not touching on that in my review. Let's get to the likes...<br /><br />LIKES: 1) The threads of love and redemption woven into the pattern of these books brought about an unexpected emotional response in me. That doesn't happen very often and I give a lot of credit to Gemmell for a unique but touching story. The redemptive storylines in this book sealed a 4-star rating for me. It also leaves me to wonder, was the plot constructed around this to lend more weight to the emotional undercurrents? 2) These characters are complex, gritty, and very human. It's interesting that two of my favorite authors, Robert Jordan and David Gemmell, both excel at developing rich characters but do so with such different styles, i.e. Heavy handed and subtle approaches, respectively. Most of the characters in these two books suck you in, even if some aren't very likable. Some also go through transformations in the book (several actually change their names to signify the transformations). He does this even though the main characters in each book are not the same, though the major players in the first book definitely play roles in Last Sword of Power. 3) Typical Gemmell traits that I always enjoy... Gritty battle scenes, heroic stands against evil, etc.<br /><br />DISLIKES: 1) The plot was all over the place and overall it's just not that interesting, in my opinion. 2) Weaving actual historical events and characters into the story was mostly a distraction, but there were some cool elements. 3) The magic system feels pretty boring and cliche, again not very interesting. 4) The antagonist in Last Sword of Power feels a little one dimensional amidst such rich protagonists and supporting characters, even compared to the antagonist in Ghost King. It led me to wonder what more could have been done there.<br /><br />CONTENT: (Violence) - As usual for Gemmell, there was a fair amount of violence, nothing gratuitous but war is depicted in detail; however, not glamorized. (Language) - Very little, no strong language. (Sex) - Some sex scenes, with little detail; also some rape scenes and references but never anything graphic with the sexual content.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10387505482127657507">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1006602439">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1006602439" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/33358575-francesco-manno" class="left imgcol" title="Francesco Manno"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442990793p2/33358575.jpg" alt="Francesco Manno" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1006602439?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 17, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/33358575-francesco-manno" class="user" title="Francesco Manno">Francesco Manno</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/781301.Last_Sword_of_Power" title="Paperback 9780345379016" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1006602439">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11145845971185064015"><a rel="nofollow" href="http://panopticonitalia.blogspot.it/2014/05/lultima-spada-del-potere-di-david.html" target="_blank">http://panopticonitalia.blogspot.it/2...</a><br /><br />With this novel closes the sub-cycle of the Stones of Power.<br />As the king of ghosts, the last sword of power is a fantasy in which David Gemmell draws from the Breton Cycle, but it does stravolgendolo and inserting elements related to Greek mythology and Norse, which make the story even more fun.<br />On one side are narrated the events relating to Britain after the abandonment by the Romans, on the other hand the author leads us directly to Hell, in a parallel un</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11145845971185064015"><a rel="nofollow" href="http://panopticonitalia.blogspot.it/2014/05/lultima-spada-del-potere-di-david.html" target="_blank">http://panopticonitalia.blogspot.it/2...</a><br /><br />With this novel closes the sub-cycle of the Stones of Power.<br />As the king of ghosts, the last sword of power is a fantasy in which David Gemmell draws from the Breton Cycle, but it does stravolgendolo and inserting elements related to Greek mythology and Norse, which make the story even more fun.<br />On one side are narrated the events relating to Britain after the abandonment by the Romans, on the other hand the author leads us directly to Hell, in a parallel universe where to lord are the demons, and in which our protagonists they will fight for their very souls.<br />The magic plays a fundamental role in this story. They became the pivot of the book the Stones of Power, the Sipstrassi, able to implement any kind of witchcraft, if used properly, even to lead a man from another universe. Then we have the Sword of Cunobelin that provides its holder the great powers, including clairvoyance. Paradigmatic also is the fact that the main antagonist of Uther is Wotan, a malevolent deity that has the right to move between the real world and the Underworld.<br />Even with great care for the magical element, that does not mean that Gemmell has deprived us of the wars in which he describes in detail the military tactics adopted by the armies in the fight, as well as great importance is given to the melee combat in which exalt the heroes.<br />The book is full of new characters, but also the old make their appearance, playing an important role in the story and as usual until the last page, it is not clear what are their real intentions. Among the new, noteworthy is Cormac, son of Uther, abandoned in a cave to a sad fate, grew up in poverty and unaware of being the rightful heir to the throne, who will choose to go down to the underworld to save his beloved and his father eternal oblivion.<br />As for the old characters, however, even in this book appears Culain (in the role of Lancelot) that protector of Uther, became his bitter enemy to the fact that he slept with his wife, Laitha.<br />Basically, this too, as the king of ghosts, is an excellent book that I recommend reading if you are fond of sword and sorcery.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11145845971185064015">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13563773435223331089">Following on from <em>Ghost King</em>, <em>Last Sword of Power</em> focuses on the more familiar elements of the Arthurian legend: of Guinevere and Lancelot's betrayal (which happens 'between' books), of Uther's son raised without knowing who he is, of Morgana, of Uther (NOT Arthur) on the isle of Avalon - although it is given a different name here - and of Uther's (again, NOT Arthur's) final battle.<br /><br />Like <em>Ghost King</em>, this novel again makes use of the Siptrassi stones to provide the rationale behind the magic. <br /><br />Of t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13563773435223331089">Following on from <em>Ghost King</em>, <em>Last Sword of Power</em> focuses on the more familiar elements of the Arthurian legend: of Guinevere and Lancelot's betrayal (which happens 'between' books), of Uther's son raised without knowing who he is, of Morgana, of Uther (NOT Arthur) on the isle of Avalon - although it is given a different name here - and of Uther's (again, NOT Arthur's) final battle.<br /><br />Like <em>Ghost King</em>, this novel again makes use of the Siptrassi stones to provide the rationale behind the magic. <br /><br />Of the two Siptrassi books, I found this to be the more enjoyable.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_316744960">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/316744960" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/8883974-tinamarie" class="left imgcol" title="Tinamarie"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1347435798p2/8883974.jpg" alt="Tinamarie" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/316744960?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 24, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/8883974-tinamarie" class="user" title="Tinamarie">Tinamarie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/781301.Last_Sword_of_Power" title="Paperback 9780345379016" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer316744960">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4228186574848001112">Thuro is the typical anti-hero, a mere boy who wants to be a scholar but has to become a warrior and a leader dealing with difficult decisions. He not only has to fight his fellow humans but also immortals, who more often play a cruel game than help the mortals with their Stones of Power, and savage magical creatures. <br /><br />These may not be Gemmell's best books, but enjoy them You may. <br /></span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  <a href="/user/show/4061431-alex-jones" class="left imgcol" title="Alex Jones"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1280150642p2/4061431.jpg" alt="Alex Jones" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <a href="/user/show/4061431-alex-jones" class="user" title="Alex Jones">Alex Jones</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1850094.Last_Sword_of_Power" title="Paperback 9781857237979" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer517396079">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14189499840550552889">It is by David Gemmell, of course I absolutely loved it. I don't know what it is about his books that I enjoy so much, but even when the plot and writing borders between good and great the finished product is always so much better than the combination of everything else.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer27673731">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17603480121887451683">I hesitated a bit at reading the Jon Shannow books because they looked like they'd be in a more modern setting, and they are, with guns. However, I came to like the Shannow character as well as any of Gemmell's heroes and much enjoyed the whole set of Shannow books.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <a href="/user/show/4515830-debby-allen" class="left imgcol" title="Debby Allen"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="Debby Allen" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/129849874?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 09, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4515830-debby-allen" class="user" title="Debby Allen">Debby Allen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/781301.Last_Sword_of_Power" title="Paperback 9780345379016" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer129849874">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13777735996508004534">Better than Ghost King, mainly because Gemmell isn't constrained by the existing myth. It's still a stretch, but his storytelling skill are growing. Unlike Vonnegut, his progress is consistent. Reading them in order is interesting.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('/J3jPmFMukdh0nhGFBqXT6BaIoWJZR8IXfMLt9CetS6ZSdztk56uve0KDP1qe3H96a3hnMC4WKI3+g4lHAtDaw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3iQHXD/sV0JQZHu5nXWQ7htlkhfHsl4dd+fkOCtIvTe78DiPzT5DuNy8DwLjFHZcUpJRDo5vGbcd7uGq591Lcg==')})

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/11586.David_Gemmell">About David Gemmell</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/11586.David_Gemmell"><img alt="11586" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1202771023p2/11586.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer3209187200633276162">David Andrew Gemmell was a bestselling British author of heroic fantasy. A former journalist and newspaper editor, Gemmell had his first work of fiction published in 1984. He went on to write over thirty novels. Best known for his debut, Legend, Gemmell's works display violence, yet also explores themes in honour, loyalty and redemption. With over one million copies sold, his work continues to sel</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3209187200633276162">David Andrew Gemmell was a bestselling British author of heroic fantasy. A former journalist and newspaper editor, Gemmell had his first work of fiction published in 1984. He went on to write over thirty novels. Best known for his debut, Legend, Gemmell's works display violence, yet also explores themes in honour, loyalty and redemption. With over one million copies sold, his work continues to sell worldwide.</span>
